## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (ordinary differential equation rate laws)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is an instantaneous rate of change of concentration A with time t, which is the standard setup for kinetic rate-law discovery in chemical reaction engineering and physical chemistry. With only (t, A) available, the most likely relationships are mass-action-type rate laws in A and/or time-varying effective rate constants k(t).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (rate independent of A; e.g., surface-limited with excess reactant)
- Zero-order with constant source/sink: dA_dt = c0 + c1 (net constant production/consumption over the window)
- First-order decay (mass-action): dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay or pseudo-first-order conditions)
- First-order approach to equilibrium: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (relaxation toward equilibrium concentration c1)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular self-reaction or 2A -> products)
- General power-law (nth-order): dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical/global rate law fitting over limited range)
- Offset power-law: dA_dt = -c0 * (A + c1)**c2 (effective concentration shift due to background/measurement offset)
- Autocatalytic / logistic-type: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-acceleration with saturation/finite capacity)
- Substrate/product inhibition (rational): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (rate limited by site saturation or inhibition-like effect)
- Higher-order with inhibition: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 / (A + c1) (mixed mass-action and saturation limitation)
- Time-varying first-order (accelerating): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (effective rate constant increases with time)
- Time-varying first-order (deactivating): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (effective rate constant decreases with time)
- Biexponential effective rate constant: dA_dt = -A * (c0 + c1 * exp(-c2 * t)) (fast transient plus steady decay component)
- Periodically forced kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * A (modulated rate due to periodic illumination/feeds)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Consumption-only kinetics typically imply dA_dt ≤ 0 for A ≥ 0, often realized by a leading negative sign times a nonnegative function of A and t.
- If dA_dt depends only on A (no explicit t), the system is autonomous; trajectories collapse onto a single phase curve and integrated rate laws are often simple (e.g., ln(A) vs t linear for first-order).
- Linear dependence dA_dt ∝ A indicates exponential decay in A(t); deviations from linearity in A suggest multi-molecular steps or changing mechanism/conditions.
- Quadratic or higher polynomial dependence in A indicates mass-action with multiple reactants effectively proportional to A, often producing curvature in ln(A) vs t but linearity in 1/A or A^(1-n) plots.
- A term of the form -(A - c1) implies relaxation toward a nonzero steady state (equilibrium or buffered concentration) rather than decay to zero.
- Rational forms like A/(A + c) indicate saturation of an intermediate or finite-capacity limitation; the rate becomes approximately constant at high A and proportional to A at low A.
- Multiplicative exp(±c*t) on an A-dependent rate indicates time-varying effective rate constants (e.g., catalyst activation/deactivation, changing conditions) without introducing additional state variables.
- Products like A*(c1 - A) indicate self-accelerating production at low A with limiting capacity at high A (autocatalysis with depletion/constraint).
- Additive constant terms in dA_dt (e.g., -c0) suggest zero-order regimes, external feed/bleed, or background processes not proportional to A.
